Prix</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Andreas Nikolaus Lauda</b> (22 February 1949&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 20 May 2019) was an <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_drivers_from_Austria" title="Formula One drivers from Austria">Austrian Formula One driver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a> entrepreneur. He was a three-time <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Drivers%27_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Drivers&#39; Champions">F1 World Drivers\' Champion</a>, winning in <a href="/wiki/1975_Formula_One_season" title="1975 Formula One season">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1977_Formula_One_season" title="1977 Formula One season">1977</a> and <a href="/wiki/1984_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="1984 Formula One World Championship">1984</a>, and is the only driver in F1 history to have been champion for both <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> and <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a>, the sport\'s two most successful constructors.\n</p><p>As an aviation entrepreneur, he founded and ran three airlines: <a href="/wiki/Lauda_Air" title="Lauda Air">Lauda Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lauda_(airline)" title="Lauda (airline)">Lauda</a>. He was a Bombardier Business Aircraft brand ambassador. He was also a consultant for <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Scuderia Ferrari</a> and team manager of the <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Racing" title="Jaguar Racing">Jaguar</a> Formula One racing team for two years. Afterwards, he worked as a pundit for German TV during Grand Prix weekends and acted as non-executive chairman of <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_in_Formula_One" title="Mercedes-Benz in Formula One">Mercedes-AMG Petronas Motorsport</a>, of which Lauda owned 10%.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Having emerged as Formula One\'s star driver amid a <a href="/wiki/1975_Formula_One_season" title="1975 Formula One season">1975</a> title win and leading the <a href="/wiki/1976_Formula_One_season" title="1976 Formula One season">1976</a> championship battle, Lauda was seriously injured in a crash at the <a href="/wiki/1976_German_Grand_Prix" title="1976 German Grand Prix">1976 German Grand Prix</a> at the <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="N\xc3\xbcrburgring">N\xc3\xbcrburgring</a> during which his <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_312T#312T2_(1976)/312T2B_(1977-1978)" title="Ferrari 312T">Ferrari 312T2</a> burst into flames, and he came close to death after inhaling hot toxic fumes and suffering severe burns.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He survived and recovered sufficiently to race again just six weeks later at the <a href="/wiki/1976_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="1976 Italian Grand Prix">Italian Grand Prix</a>. Although he lost that year\'s title&#160;&#8211;&#32;by just one point&#160;&#8211;&#32;to <a href="/wiki/James_Hunt" title="James Hunt">James Hunt</a>, he won his second championship the year after, during his final season at Ferrari. After a couple of years at <a href="/wiki/Brabham" title="Brabham">Brabham</a> and two years\' hiatus, Lauda returned and raced four seasons for McLaren between 1982 and 1985 \xe2\x80\x93 during which he won the <a href="/wiki/1984_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="1984 Formula One World Championship">1984</a> title by half a point over his teammate <a href="/wiki/Alain_Prost" title="Alain Prost">Alain Prost</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_in_racing">Early years in racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early years in racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lauda,_Niki_1973-07-06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Lauda%2C_Niki_1973-07-06.jpg/170px-Lauda%2C_Niki_1973-07-06.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Lauda%2C_Niki_1973-07-06.jpg/255px-Lauda%2C_Niki_1973-07-06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Lauda%2C_Niki_1973-07-06.jpg/340px-Lauda%2C_Niki_1973-07-06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="444" data-file-height="662" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lauda,_Niki_1973-07-06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lauda at the <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="N\xc3\xbcrburgring">N\xc3\xbcrburgring</a> in <a href="/wiki/1973_Formula_One_season" title="1973 Formula One season">1973</a>, three years before his accident</div></div></div>\n<p>Niki Lauda was born on 22 February 1949 in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, Austria, to a wealthy paper manufacturing family.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Moulson_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moulson-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> His paternal grandfather was the Viennese-born industrialist <a href="/wiki/Hans_Lauda" title="Hans Lauda">Hans Lauda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aeiou_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aeiou-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-die-namenslosen_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-die-namenslosen-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lauda became a racing driver despite his family\'s disapproval.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> After starting out with a <a href="/wiki/Mini" title="Mini">Mini</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Lauda moved on into <a href="/wiki/Formula_Vee" title="Formula Vee">Formula Vee</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> as was normal in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, but rapidly moved up to drive in private <a href="/wiki/Porsche_in_motorsport" title="Porsche in motorsport">Porsche</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Cars_Ltd" title="Chevron Cars Ltd">Chevron</a> sports cars.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> With his career stalled, he took out a <a href="/wiki/British_pound" class="mw-redirect" title="British pound">\xc2\xa3</a>30,000 bank loan,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> secured by a life insurance policy, to buy his way into the fledgling <a href="/wiki/March_Engineering" title="March Engineering">March</a> team as a <a href="/wiki/Formula_Two" title="Formula Two">Formula Two</a> (F2) driver in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Because of his family\'s disapproval he had an ongoing feud with them over his racing ambitions and abandoned further contact.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lauda was quickly promoted to the F1 team, but drove for March in F1 and F2 in 1972. Although the F2 cars were good (and Lauda\'s driving skills impressed March principal Robin Herd), March\'s 1972 F1 season was catastrophic. Perhaps the lowest point of the team\'s season came at the Canadian Grand Prix at Mosport Park, where both March cars were disqualified within 3 laps of each other after just past 3/4 race distance. Lauda took out another bank loan to buy his way into the <a href="/wiki/British_Racing_Motors" title="British Racing Motors">BRM</a> team in 1973. Lauda was instantly quick, but the team was in decline; although the BRM P160E was quick and easy to drive it was not reliable and its engine lacked power. Lauda\xe2\x80\x99s big break came after he ran 3rd at the Monaco Grand Prix that year, and <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Ferrari" title="Enzo Ferrari">Enzo Ferrari</a> became interested. When his BRM teammate <a href="/wiki/Clay_Regazzoni" title="Clay Regazzoni">Clay Regazzoni</a> left to rejoin <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> in 1974 and team owner Enzo Ferrari asked him what he thought of Lauda. Regazzoni spoke so favourably of Lauda that Ferrari promptly signed him, paying him enough to clear his debts.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Ferrari_.281974.E2.80.931977.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferrari_(1974\xe2\x80\x931977)">Ferrari (1974\xe2\x80\x931977)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ferrari (1974\xe2\x80\x931977)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hunt%E2%80%93Lauda_rivalry" title="Hunt\xe2\x80\x93Lauda rivalry">Hunt\xe2\x80\x93Lauda rivalry</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LaudaNiki19760731Ferrari312T2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/LaudaNiki19760731Ferrari312T2.jpg/220px-LaudaNiki19760731Ferrari312T2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/LaudaNiki19760731Ferrari312T2.jpg/330px-LaudaNiki19760731Ferrari312T2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/LaudaNiki19760731Ferrari312T2.jpg/440px-LaudaNiki19760731Ferrari312T2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3396" data-file-height="2260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LaudaNiki19760731Ferrari312T2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lauda practicing at the <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="N\xc3\xbcrburgring">N\xc3\xbcrburgring</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1976_German_Grand_Prix" title="1976 German Grand Prix">1976 German Grand Prix</a></div></div></div>\n<p>After an unsuccessful start to the 1970s culminating in a disastrous start to the 1973 season, Ferrari regrouped completely under <a href="/wiki/Luca_di_Montezemolo" class="mw-redirect" title="Luca di Montezemolo">Luca di Montezemolo</a> and were resurgent in <a href="/wiki/1974_Formula_One_season" title="1974 Formula One season">1974</a>. The team\'s faith in the little-known Lauda was quickly rewarded by a second-place finish in his debut race for the team, the season-opening <a href="/wiki/1974_Argentine_Grand_Prix" title="1974 Argentine Grand Prix">Argentine Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> His first <a href="/wiki/Grand_Prix_motor_racing" title="Grand Prix motor racing">Grand Prix</a> (GP) victory \xe2\x80\x93 and the first for Ferrari since 1972 \xe2\x80\x93 followed only three races later in the <a href="/wiki/1974_Spanish_Grand_Prix" title="1974 Spanish Grand Prix">Spanish Grand Prix</a>. Although Lauda became the season\'s pacesetter, achieving six consecutive <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">pole positions</a>, a mixture of inexperience and mechanical unreliability meant Lauda won only one more race that year, the <a href="/wiki/1974_Dutch_Grand_Prix" title="1974 Dutch Grand Prix">Dutch GP</a>. He finished fourth in the Drivers\' Championship and demonstrated immense commitment to testing and improving the car.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Niki_Lauda,_1975_British_Grand_Prix.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Niki_Lauda%2C_1975_British_Grand_Prix.jpg/220px-Niki_Lauda%2C_1975_British_Grand_Prix.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Niki_Lauda%2C_1975_British_Grand_Prix.jpg/330px-Niki_Lauda%2C_1975_British_Grand_Prix.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Niki_Lauda%2C_1975_British_Grand_Prix.jpg/440px-Niki_Lauda%2C_1975_British_Grand_Prix.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1758" data-file-height="1183" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Niki_Lauda,_1975_British_Grand_Prix.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lauda in 1975</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1975_Formula_One_season" title="1975 Formula One season">1975 F1 season</a> started slowly for Lauda; after no better than a fifth-place finish in the first four races, he won four of the next five driving the new <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_312T" title="Ferrari 312T">Ferrari 312T</a>. His first World Championship was confirmed with a third-place finish at the Italian Grand Prix at Monza; Lauda\'s teammate Regazzoni won the race and Ferrari clinched their first Constructors\' Championship in 11 years; Lauda then picked up a fifth win at the last race of the year, the <a href="/wiki/1975_United_States_Grand_Prix" title="1975 United States Grand Prix">United States GP</a> at <a href="/wiki/Watkins_Glen_International" title="Watkins Glen International">Watkins Glen</a>. He also became the first driver to lap the <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="N\xc3\xbcrburgring">N\xc3\xbcrburgring</a> Nordschleife in under seven minutes, which was considered a huge feat as the Nordschleife section of the N\xc3\xbcrburgring was two miles longer than it is today. Lauda did not win the German Grand Prix from pole position there that year; after battling hard with <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Depailler" title="Patrick Depailler">Patrick Depailler</a> for the lead for the first half of the race, Lauda led for the first 9 laps but suffered a puncture at the Wippermann 9 miles into the 10th lap and was passed by <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Reutemann" title="Carlos Reutemann">Carlos Reutemann</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Hunt" title="James Hunt">James Hunt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Pryce" title="Tom Pryce">Tom Pryce</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Laffite" title="Jacques Laffite">Jacques Laffite</a>; Lauda made it back to the pits with a damaged front wing and a destroyed left front tyre. The Ferrari pit changed the destroyed tyre and Lauda managed to make it to the podium in 3rd behind Reutemann and Laffite after Hunt retired and Pryce had to slow down because of a fuel leak. Lauda was known for giving away any trophies he won to his local garage in exchange for his car to be washed and serviced.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Unlike 1975 and despite tensions between Lauda and Montezemolo\'s successor, <a href="/wiki/Daniele_Audetto" title="Daniele Audetto">Daniele Audetto</a>, Lauda dominated the start of the <a href="/wiki/1976_Formula_One_season" title="1976 Formula One season">1976 F1 season</a>, winning four of the first six races and finishing second in the other two. By the time of his fifth win of the year at the <a href="/wiki/1976_British_Grand_Prix" title="1976 British Grand Prix">British GP</a>, he had more than double the points of his closest challengers <a href="/wiki/Jody_Scheckter" title="Jody Scheckter">Jody Scheckter</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Hunt" title="James Hunt">James Hunt</a>, and a second consecutive World Championship appeared a formality. It would be a feat not achieved since <a href="/wiki/Jack_Brabham" title="Jack Brabham">Jack Brabham</a>\'s victories in <a href="/wiki/1959_Formula_One_season" title="1959 Formula One season">1959</a> and <a href="/wiki/1960_Formula_One_season" title="1960 Formula One season">1960</a>. He also looked set to win the most races in a season, a record held by the late <a href="/wiki/Jim_Clark" title="Jim Clark">Jim Clark</a> since <a href="/wiki/1963_Formula_One_season" title="1963 Formula One season">1963</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1976_N.C3.BCrburgring_crash"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1976_N\xc3\xbcrburgring_crash">1976 N\xc3\xbcrburgring crash</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1976 N\xc3\xbcrburgring crash">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A week before the <a href="/wiki/1976_German_Grand_Prix" title="1976 German Grand Prix">1976 German Grand Prix</a> at the <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="N\xc3\xbcrburgring">N\xc3\xbcrburgring</a>, even though he was the fastest driver on that circuit at the time, Lauda urged his fellow drivers to boycott the race, largely because of the 23-kilometre (14&#160;mi) circuit\'s safety arrangements, citing the organisers\' lack of resources to properly manage such a huge circuit, including lack of fire marshals, fire and safety equipment and safety vehicles.  Formula One was quite dangerous at the time (three of the drivers that day would later die in Formula One incidents: <a href="/wiki/Tom_Pryce" title="Tom Pryce">Tom Pryce</a> in 1977; <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Peterson" title="Ronnie Peterson">Ronnie Peterson</a> in 1978; and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Depailler" title="Patrick Depailler">Patrick Depailler</a> in 1980), but a majority of the drivers voted against the boycott and the race went ahead.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lauda_accidente2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Lauda_accidente2.jpg/220px-Lauda_accidente2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Lauda_accidente2.jpg/330px-Lauda_accidente2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Lauda_accidente2.jpg/440px-Lauda_accidente2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1140" data-file-height="759" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lauda_accidente2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lauda\'s car on fire</div></div></div>\n<p>On 1 August 1976 during the second lap at the very fast left kink before Bergwerk, Lauda was involved in an accident where his Ferrari swerved off the track, hit an embankment, burst into flames, and made contact with <a href="/wiki/Brett_Lunger" title="Brett Lunger">Brett Lunger</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Surtees" title="Surtees">Surtees</a>-<a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a> car. Unlike Lunger, Lauda was trapped in the wreckage. Drivers <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Merzario" title="Arturo Merzario">Arturo Merzario</a>, Lunger, <a href="/wiki/Guy_Edwards" title="Guy Edwards">Guy Edwards</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harald_Ertl" title="Harald Ertl">Harald Ertl</a> arrived at the scene a few moments later, but before Merzario was able to pull Lauda from his car, he suffered severe burns to his head and inhaled hot toxic gases that damaged his lungs and blood.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>  In an interview with BBC Radio 5 Live ("I Was There -- May 21, 2019"; "Niki Lauda speaks in 2015"), Lauda said, "...there were basically two or three drivers trying to get me out of the car, but one was Arturo Merzario, the Italian guy, who also had to stop there at the scene, because I blocked the road; and he really came into the car himself, and uh, triggered my, my seatbelt loose, and then pulled me out.  It was unbelievable, how he could do that, and I met him afterwards, and I said, \'How could you do it?!\'.  He said, \'Honestly, I do not know, but to open your seatbelt was so difficult, because you were pushing so hard against it, and when it was open, I got you out of the car like a feather...\'."<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>  As Lauda was wearing a modified helmet, it didn\'t fit him properly; the foam had compressed and it slid off his head after the accident, leaving his face exposed to the fire.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Although Lauda was conscious and able to stand immediately after the accident, he later lapsed into a coma.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> While in hospital he was given the <a href="/wiki/Last_rites" title="Last rites">last rites</a>, but survived.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lauda suffered extensive scarring from the burns to his head, losing most of his right ear as well as the hair on the right side of his head, his eyebrows, and his eyelids. He chose to limit reconstructive surgery to replacing the eyelids and getting them to work properly. After the accident he always wore a cap to cover the scars on his head. He arranged for sponsors to use the cap for advertising.\n</p><p>With Lauda out of the contest, Carlos Reutemann was taken on as his replacement. Ferrari boycotted the <a href="/wiki/1976_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="1976 Austrian Grand Prix">Austrian Grand Prix</a> in protest at what they saw as preferential treatment shown towards <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a> driver <a href="/wiki/James_Hunt" title="James Hunt">James Hunt</a> at the Spanish and British Grands Prix.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_racing">Return to racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Return to racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lauda missed only two races, appearing at the Monza press conference six weeks after the accident with his fresh burns still bandaged. He finished fourth in the <a href="/wiki/1976_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="1976 Italian Grand Prix">Italian GP</a>, despite being, by his own admission, absolutely petrified. F1 journalist <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Roebuck" title="Nigel Roebuck">Nigel Roebuck</a> recalls seeing Lauda in the pits, peeling the blood-soaked bandages off his scarred scalp. He also had to wear a specially adapted crash helmet so as to not be in too much discomfort. In Lauda\'s absence, Hunt had mounted a late charge to reduce Lauda\'s lead in the World Championship standings. Hunt and Lauda were friends away from the circuit, and their personal on-track rivalry, while intense, was cleanly contested and fair. Following wins in the <a href="/wiki/1976_Canadian_Grand_Prix" title="1976 Canadian Grand Prix">Canadian</a> and <a href="/wiki/1976_United_States_Grand_Prix" title="1976 United States Grand Prix">United States</a> Grands Prix, Hunt stood only three points behind Lauda before the final race of the season, the <a href="/wiki/1976_Japanese_Grand_Prix" title="1976 Japanese Grand Prix">Japanese Grand Prix</a>.\n</p><p>Lauda qualified third, one place behind Hunt, but on race day there was torrential rain and Lauda retired after two laps. He later said that he felt it was unsafe to continue under these conditions, especially since his eyes were watering excessively because of his fire-damaged tear ducts and inability to blink. Hunt led much of the race before his tires blistered and a pit stop dropped him down the order. He recovered to third, thus winning the title by a single point.\n</p><p>Lauda\'s previously good relationship with Ferrari was severely affected by his decision to withdraw from the Japanese Grand Prix, and he endured a difficult <a href="/wiki/1977_Formula_One_season" title="1977 Formula One season">1977 season</a>, despite easily winning the championship through consistency rather than outright pace. Lauda disliked his new teammate, Reutemann, who had served as his replacement driver. Lauda was not comfortable with this move and felt he had been let down by Ferrari. "We never could stand each other, and instead of taking pressure off me, they put on even more by bringing Carlos Reutemann into the team."<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Having announced his decision to quit Ferrari at season\'s end, Lauda left earlier after he won the Drivers\' Championship at the <a href="/wiki/1977_United_States_Grand_Prix" title="1977 United States Grand Prix">United States Grand Prix</a>  because of the team\'s decision to run the unknown <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Villeneuve" title="Gilles Villeneuve">Gilles Villeneuve</a> in a third car at the <a href="/wiki/1977_Canadian_Grand_Prix" title="1977 Canadian Grand Prix">Canadian Grand Prix</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Brabham_and_first_retirement_.281978.E2.80.931979.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Brabham_and_first_retirement_(1978\xe2\x80\x931979)">Brabham and first retirement (1978\xe2\x80\x931979)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Brabham and first retirement (1978\xe2\x80\x931979)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lauda_at_1978_Dutch_Grand_Prix_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Lauda_at_1978_Dutch_Grand_Prix_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Lauda_at_1978_Dutch_Grand_Prix_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Lauda_at_1978_Dutch_Grand_Prix_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Lauda_at_1978_Dutch_Grand_Prix_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Lauda_at_1978_Dutch_Grand_Prix_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Lauda_at_1978_Dutch_Grand_Prix_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2050" data-file-height="1250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lauda_at_1978_Dutch_Grand_Prix_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lauda in the <a href="/wiki/Brabham" title="Brabham">Brabham</a>-<a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_in_Formula_One" title="Alfa Romeo in Formula One">Alfa Romeo</a> at Zandvoort (1978)</div></div></div><p>Joining Parmalat-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Brabham" title="Brabham">Brabham</a>-<a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_in_Formula_One" title="Alfa Romeo in Formula One">Alfa Romeo</a> in 1978 for a $1&#160;million salary, Lauda endured two unsuccessful seasons, remembered mainly for his one race in the <a href="/wiki/Brabham_BT46" title="Brabham BT46">Brabham BT46B</a>, a radical design known as the Fan Car: it won its first and only race at the Swedish GP, but Brabham did not use the car in F1 again; other teams vigorously protested the fan car\'s legality and Brabham team owner <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Ecclestone" title="Bernie Ecclestone">Bernie Ecclestone</a>, who at the time was maneuvering for acquisition of Formula One\'s commercial rights, did not want to fight a protracted battle over the car, but the victory in Sweden remained official. The Brabham BT46 Alfa Romeo flat-12 began the 1978 season at the third race in South Africa. It suffered from a variety of troubles that forced Lauda to retire the car 9 out of 14 races. Lauda\'s best results, apart from the wins in Sweden and Italy after the penalization of Mario Andretti and Gilles Villeneuve, were 2nd in Monaco and Great Britain, and a 3rd in the Netherlands.\n</p><p>The Alfa flat-12 engine was too wide for ground effect designs in that the opposed cylinder banks impeded with the venturi tunnels, so Alfa designed a V12 for 1979. It was the fourth 12-cylinder engine design that propelled the Austrian in F1 since 1973. Lauda\'s 1979 F1 season was again marred by retirements and poor pace, even though he won the non-championship <a href="/wiki/1979_Dino_Ferrari_Grand_Prix" title="1979 Dino Ferrari Grand Prix">1979 Dino Ferrari Grand Prix</a> with the Brabham-Alfa. In the single-make <a href="/wiki/BMW_M1_Procar_Championship" title="BMW M1 Procar Championship">BMW M1 Procar Championship</a>, driving for the British Formula Two team <a href="/wiki/Project_Four_Racing" title="Project Four Racing">Project Four Racing</a> (led by <a href="/wiki/Ron_Dennis" title="Ron Dennis">Ron Dennis</a>) when not in a factory entry, Lauda won three races for P4 plus the series. Decades later, Lauda won a BMW Procar exhibition race event before the <a href="/wiki/2008_German_Grand_Prix" title="2008 German Grand Prix">2008 German Grand Prix</a>.\n</p><p>In September, Lauda finished 4th in Monza, and won the non-WC Imola event, still with the Alfa V12 engine. After that, Brabham returned to the familiar Cosworth V8. In late September, during practice for the <a href="/wiki/1979_Canadian_Grand_Prix" title="1979 Canadian Grand Prix">1979 Canadian Grand Prix</a>, Lauda cut short a practice session and promptly informed team principal Ecclestone, that he wished to retire immediately, as he had no more desire to "continue the silliness of driving around in circles". Lauda, who in the meantime had founded Lauda Air, a charter airline, returned to Austria to run the company full-time.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSportObit_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCSportObit-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="McLaren_comeback.2C_third_world_title.2C_and_second_retirement_.281982.E2.80.931985.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="McLaren_comeback,_third_world_title,_and_second_retirement_(1982\xe2\x80\x931985)">McLaren comeback, third world title, and second retirement (1982\xe2\x80\x931985)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: McLaren comeback, third world title, and second retirement (1982\xe2\x80\x931985)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lauda_McLaren_MP4-2_1984_Dallas_F1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Lauda_McLaren_MP4-2_1984_Dallas_F1.jpg/220px-Lauda_McLaren_MP4-2_1984_Dallas_F1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Lauda_McLaren_MP4-2_1984_Dallas_F1.jpg/330px-Lauda_McLaren_MP4-2_1984_Dallas_F1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Lauda_McLaren_MP4-2_1984_Dallas_F1.jpg/440px-Lauda_McLaren_MP4-2_1984_Dallas_F1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1055" data-file-height="606" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lauda_McLaren_MP4-2_1984_Dallas_F1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Five years after his first retirement, Lauda won his third title driving a <a href="/wiki/McLaren_MP4/2" title="McLaren MP4/2">McLaren MP4/2</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1982 Lauda returned to racing, for an unprecedented $3&#160;million salary.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCSportObit_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCSportObit-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> After a successful test with <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a>, the only problem was to convince then team sponsor <a href="/wiki/Marlboro_(cigarette)" title="Marlboro (cigarette)">Marlboro</a> that he was still capable of winning. Lauda proved he was when, in his third race back, he won the <a href="/wiki/1982_United_States_Grand_Prix_West" title="1982 United States Grand Prix West">Long Beach Grand Prix</a>. Before the opening race of the season at <a href="/wiki/Kyalami" title="Kyalami">Kyalami</a> race track in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, Lauda was the organiser of the so-called "drivers\' strike"; Lauda had seen that the new <a href="/wiki/FIA_Super_Licence" title="FIA Super Licence">Super Licence</a> required the drivers to commit themselves to their present teams and realised that this could hinder a driver\'s negotiating position. The drivers, with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Teo_Fabi" title="Teo Fabi">Teo Fabi</a>, barricaded themselves in a banqueting suite at Sunnyside Park Hotel until they had won the day.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1983 season proved to be transitional for the McLaren team as they were making a change from <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a>-<a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a> engines, to <a href="/wiki/Techniques_d%27Avant_Garde" title="Techniques d&#39;Avant Garde">TAG</a>-badged <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> turbo engines, and Lauda did not win a race that year, with his best finish being second at Long Beach behind his teammate <a href="/wiki/John_Watson_(racing_driver)" title="John Watson (racing driver)">John Watson</a>. Some political maneuvering by Lauda forced a furious chief designer <a href="/wiki/John_Barnard" title="John Barnard">John Barnard</a> to design an interim car earlier than expected to get the TAG-Porsche engine some much-needed race testing; Lauda nearly won the last race of the season in South Africa.\n</p><p>Lauda won a third world championship in <a href="/wiki/1984_Formula_One_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1984 Formula One season">1984</a> by half a point over teammate <a href="/wiki/Alain_Prost" title="Alain Prost">Alain Prost</a>, due only to half points being awarded for the shortened <a href="/wiki/1984_Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="1984 Monaco Grand Prix">1984 Monaco Grand Prix</a>. His <a href="/wiki/1984_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="1984 Austrian Grand Prix">Austrian Grand Prix</a> victory that year is so far the only time an Austrian has won his home Grand Prix.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Initially, Lauda did not want Prost to become his teammate, as he presented a much faster rival. However, during the two seasons together, they had a good relationship and Lauda later said that beating the talented Frenchman was a big motivator for him.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The whole season continued to be dominated by Lauda and Prost, who won 12 of 16 races. Lauda won five races, while Prost won seven. However, Lauda, who set a record for the most pole positions in a season during the 1975 season, rarely matched his teammate in qualifying. Despite this, Lauda\'s championship win came in <a href="/wiki/1984_Portuguese_Grand_Prix" title="1984 Portuguese Grand Prix">Portugal</a>, when he had to start in eleventh place on the grid, while Prost qualified on the front row. Prost did everything he could, starting from second and winning his seventh race of the season, but Lauda\'s calculating drive (which included setting the fastest race lap), passing car after car, saw him finish second behind his teammate which gave him enough points to win his third title.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> His second place was a lucky one though as <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Mansell" title="Nigel Mansell">Nigel Mansell</a> was in second for much of the race. However, as it was his last race with <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus" title="Team Lotus">Lotus</a> before joining <a href="/wiki/WilliamsF1" class="mw-redirect" title="WilliamsF1">Williams</a> in 1985, Lotus boss <a href="/wiki/Peter_Warr" title="Peter Warr">Peter Warr</a> refused to give Mansell the brakes he wanted for <a href="/wiki/Lotus_95T" title="Lotus 95T">his car</a> and the Englishman retired with brake failure on lap 52. As Lauda had passed the <a href="/wiki/Toleman_TG184" title="Toleman TG184">Toleman</a> of F1 rookie <a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">Ayrton Senna</a> for third place only a few laps earlier, Mansell\'s retirement elevated him to second behind Prost.\n</p><p>The 1985 season was a disappointment for Lauda, with eleven retirements from the fourteen races he started. He did not start the <a href="/wiki/1985_Belgian_Grand_Prix" title="1985 Belgian Grand Prix">Belgian Grand Prix</a> at <a href="/wiki/Circuit_de_Spa-Francorchamps" title="Circuit de Spa-Francorchamps">Spa-Francorchamps</a> after crashing and breaking his wrist during practice, and he later missed the <a href="/wiki/1985_European_Grand_Prix" title="1985 European Grand Prix">European Grand Prix</a> at <a href="/wiki/Brands_Hatch" title="Brands Hatch">Brands Hatch</a>; John Watson replaced him for that race. He did manage fourth at the <a href="/wiki/1985_San_Marino_Grand_Prix" title="1985 San Marino Grand Prix">San Marino Grand Prix</a>, 5th at the <a href="/wiki/1985_German_Grand_Prix" title="1985 German Grand Prix">German Grand Prix</a>, and a single race win at the <a href="/wiki/1985_Dutch_Grand_Prix" title="1985 Dutch Grand Prix">Dutch Grand Prix</a> where he held off a fast-finishing Prost late in the race. This proved to be his last Grand Prix victory and also the last Formula One Grand Prix held in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. After announcing his impending retirement at the <a href="/wiki/1985_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="1985 Austrian Grand Prix">1985 Austrian Grand Prix</a>, he retired for good at the end of that season.\n</p><p>Lauda\'s final Formula One Grand Prix drive was the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Australian_Grand_Prix" title="Australian Grand Prix">Australian Grand Prix</a> in <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>. After qualifying 16th, a steady drive saw him leading by lap 53. However, the McLaren\'s ceramic brakes suffered on the <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Street_Circuit" title="Adelaide Street Circuit">street circuit</a> and he crashed out of the lead at the end of the long Brabham Straight on lap 57 when his brakes finally failed. He was one of only two drivers in the race who had driven in the non-championship <a href="/wiki/1984_Australian_Grand_Prix" title="1984 Australian Grand Prix">1984 Australian Grand Prix</a>, the other being <a href="/wiki/1982_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="1982 Formula One World Championship">1982</a> World Champion <a href="/wiki/Keke_Rosberg" title="Keke Rosberg">Keke Rosberg</a>, who won in Adelaide in 1985 and would take Lauda\'s place at McLaren in 1986.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Niki_Lauda_helmet_Museo_Ferrari.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Niki_Lauda_helmet_Museo_Ferrari.jpg/220px-Niki_Lauda_helmet_Museo_Ferrari.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Niki_Lauda_helmet_Museo_Ferrari.jpg/330px-Niki_Lauda_helmet_Museo_Ferrari.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Niki_Lauda_helmet_Museo_Ferrari.jpg/440px-Niki_Lauda_helmet_Museo_Ferrari.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="2560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Niki_Lauda_helmet_Museo_Ferrari.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lauda\'s helmet from the 1970s, at the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Ferrari" title="Museo Ferrari">Museo Ferrari</a> in Maranello</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Helmet">Helmet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Helmet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lauda\'s helmet was originally a plain red with his full name written on both sides and the <a href="/wiki/Raiffeisen_Bank_International" title="Raiffeisen Bank International">Raiffeisen Bank</a> logo in the chin area. He wore a modified <a href="/wiki/AGV_(helmet_manufacturer)" title="AGV (helmet manufacturer)">AGV</a> helmet in the weeks following his N\xc3\xbcrburgring accident so as the lining would not aggravate his burned scalp too badly. In 1982, upon his return to McLaren, his helmet was white and featured the red "L" logo of Lauda Air instead of his name on both sides, complete with branding from his personal sponsor <a href="/wiki/Parmalat" title="Parmalat">Parmalat</a> on the top. From 1983\xe2\x80\x931985, the red and white were reversed to evoke memories of his earlier helmet design.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_management_roles">Later management roles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Later management roles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1993 Lauda returned to Formula One in a managerial position when Luca di Montezemolo offered him a consulting role at <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a>. Halfway through the 2001 season, Lauda assumed the role of team principal of the <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Racing" title="Jaguar Racing">Jaguar</a> Formula One team. The team, however, failed to improve and Lauda was made redundant, together with 70 other key figures, at the end of 2002.\n</p><p>In September 2012 he was appointed <a href="/wiki/Chairperson" title="Chairperson">non-executive chairman</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_in_Formula_One" title="Mercedes-Benz in Formula One">Mercedes AMG Petronas F1 Team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He took part in negotiations to sign <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a> to a three-year deal with Mercedes in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Roles_beyond_Formula_One">Roles beyond Formula One</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Roles beyond Formula One">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andreas_Nikolaus_Lauda_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Andreas_Nikolaus_Lauda_2011.jpg/220px-Andreas_Nikolaus_Lauda_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Andreas_Nikolaus_Lauda_2011.jpg/330px-Andreas_Nikolaus_Lauda_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Andreas_Nikolaus_Lauda_2011.jpg/440px-Andreas_Nikolaus_Lauda_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andreas_Nikolaus_Lauda_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lauda in 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>Lauda returned to running his airline, <a href="/wiki/Lauda_Air" title="Lauda Air">Lauda Air</a>, on his second Formula One retirement in 1985. During his time as airline manager, he was appointed consultant at Ferrari as part of an effort by Montezemolo to rejuvenate the team.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> After selling his Lauda Air shares to majority partner <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a> in 1999, he managed the <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Racing" title="Jaguar Racing">Jaguar</a> Formula One racing team from 2001 to 2002. In late 2003, he started a new airline, <a href="/wiki/Niki_(airline)" title="Niki (airline)">Niki</a>. Similar to Lauda Air, Niki was merged with its major partner <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> in 2011. In early 2016, Lauda took over chartered airline Amira Air and renamed the company <a href="/wiki/LaudaMotion" class="mw-redirect" title="LaudaMotion">LaudaMotion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> As a result of Air Berlin\'s insolvency in 2017, LaudaMotion took over the Niki brand and asset after an unsuccessful bid by Lufthansa and IAG.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Lauda held a commercial pilot\'s licence and from time to time acted as a captain on the flights of his airline.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/International_Motorsports_Hall_of_Fame" title="International Motorsports Hall of Fame">International Motorsports Hall of Fame</a> in 1993 and from 1996 provided commentary on Grands Prix for Austrian and German television on <a href="/wiki/RTL_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="RTL Television">RTL</a>. He was, however, criticized for calling <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kubica" title="Robert Kubica">Robert Kubica</a> a "polacke" (an ethnic slur for Polish people). It happened on air in May 2010 at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="2010 Monaco Grand Prix">Monaco Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-shortnews_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shortnews-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sport.wp.pl_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sport.wp.pl-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lauda is sometimes known by the <a href="/wiki/Nickname" title="Nickname">nickname</a> "the rat", "SuperRat" or "King Rat" because of his prominent <a href="/wiki/Malocclusion" title="Malocclusion">buck teeth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> He was associated with both <a href="/wiki/Parmalat" title="Parmalat">Parmalat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viessmann" title="Viessmann">Viessmann</a>, sponsoring the ever-present cap he wore from 1976 to hide the severe burns he sustained in his N\xc3\xbcrburgring accident. Lauda said in a 2009 interview with the German newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Zeit" title="Die Zeit">Die Zeit</a></i> that an advertiser was paying \xe2\x82\xac1.2m for the space on his red cap.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2005 the Austrian post office issued a stamp honouring him.<sup id="cite_ref-stampnews_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stampnews-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, American sports television network <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> ranked him 22nd on their top drivers of all-time.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Niki Lauda wrote five books: <i>The Art and Science of Grand Prix Driving</i> (titled <i>Formula 1: The Art and Technicalities of Grand Prix Driving</i> in some markets) (1975); <i>My Years With Ferrari</i> (1978); <i>The New Formula One: A Turbo Age</i> (1984); <i>Meine Story</i> (titled <i>To Hell and Back</i> in some markets) (1986); <i>Das dritte Leben</i> (en. <i>The third life</i>) (1996).<sup id="cite_ref-Book_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Book-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Lauda credited Austrian journalist Herbert Volker with editing the books.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television">Film and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Film and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daniel_Br%C3%BChl,_Niki_Lauda_and_Peter_Morgan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Daniel_Br%C3%BChl%2C_Niki_Lauda_and_Peter_Morgan.jpg/220px-Daniel_Br%C3%BChl%2C_Niki_Lauda_and_Peter_Morgan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Daniel_Br%C3%BChl%2C_Niki_Lauda_and_Peter_Morgan.jpg/330px-Daniel_Br%C3%BChl%2C_Niki_Lauda_and_Peter_Morgan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Daniel_Br%C3%BChl%2C_Niki_Lauda_and_Peter_Morgan.jpg/440px-Daniel_Br%C3%BChl%2C_Niki_Lauda_and_Peter_Morgan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="1908" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daniel_Br%C3%BChl,_Niki_Lauda_and_Peter_Morgan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Daniel Br\xc3\xbchl, Lauda and Peter Morgan at the premiere of <i>Rush</i> in Vienna, Austria</div></div></div>\n<p>The 1976 F1 battle between Niki Lauda and <a href="/wiki/James_Hunt" title="James Hunt">James Hunt</a> was dramatized in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Rush_(2013_film)" title="Rush (2013 film)">Rush</a></i> (2013), where Lauda was played by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Br%C3%BChl" title="Daniel Br\xc3\xbchl">Daniel Br\xc3\xbchl</a>. Lauda made a cameo appearance at the end of the film. Lauda said of Hunt\'s death, "When I heard he\'d died age 45 of a heart attack I wasn\'t surprised, I was just sad." He also said that Hunt was one of the very few he liked, a smaller number of people he respected and the only person he had envied.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lauda appeared in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Mayday_(Canadian_TV_series)" title="Mayday (Canadian TV series)">Mayday</a></i> titled "<a href="/wiki/List_of_Mayday_episodes#Season_14_.282014.29" title="List of Mayday episodes">Niki Lauda: Testing the Limits</a>" regarding the events of <a href="/wiki/Lauda_Air_Flight_004" title="Lauda Air Flight 004">Lauda Air Flight 004</a>, and described running an airline as more difficult than winning three Formula 1 championships.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name of his mother is Elisabeth.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Lauda had two sons with first wife the Chilean-Austrian Marlene Knaus (married 1976, divorced 1991): <a href="/wiki/Mathias_Lauda" title="Mathias Lauda">Mathias</a>, a race driver himself, and Lukas, who acted as Mathias\'s manager. In 2008 he married Birgit Wetzinger, a flight attendant for his airline. In 2005, she donated a kidney to Lauda when the kidney he received from his brother in 1997 failed.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In September 2009, Birgit gave birth to twins.Niki Lauda also has another son, Christoph Lauda, whose mother\'s name was not disclosed to the media.\n</p><p>On 2 August 2018 it was announced that Lauda had successfully undergone a lung transplant operation in his native Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lauda spoke fluent <a href="/wiki/Austrian_German" title="Austrian German">Austrian German</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lauda came from a Roman Catholic family. In an interview with <i>Zeit</i> he stated that he left the church for a time to avoid paying <a href="/wiki/Church_tax#Austria" title="Church tax">church taxes</a>, but went back when he had his two children baptised.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_and_legacy">Death and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Death and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On 20 May 2019, Lauda died in his sleep, aged 70, at the <a href="/wiki/University_Hospital_of_Z%C3%BCrich" title="University Hospital of Z\xc3\xbcrich">University Hospital of Z\xc3\xbcrich</a>, where he had been undergoing dialysis treatment for kidney problems, following a period of ill health.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> A statement issued on behalf of his family reported that he had died peacefully, surrounded by family members.<sup id="cite_ref-LaudetotlautSprecherin_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaudetotlautSprecherin-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Niki_Lauda_Grave_Vienna_2021.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Niki_Lauda_Grave_Vienna_2021.jpg/220px-Niki_Lauda_Grave_Vienna_2021.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Niki_Lauda_Grave_Vienna_2021.jpg/330px-Niki_Lauda_Grave_Vienna_2021.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Niki_Lauda_Grave_Vienna_2021.jpg/440px-Niki_Lauda_Grave_Vienna_2021.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="570" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Niki_Lauda_Grave_Vienna_2021.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lauda\'s grave in Vienna</div></div></div>\n<p>Various current and former drivers and teams paid tributes on social media and during the Wednesday press conference session before the <a href="/wiki/2019_Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="2019 Monaco Grand Prix">2019 Monaco Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> A moment of silence was held before the race. Throughout the weekend, fans and drivers were encouraged to wear red caps in his honour, with the Mercedes team painting their <a href="/wiki/Halo_(safety_device)" title="Halo (safety device)">halo</a> device red with a sticker stating "Niki we miss you" instead of their usual silver scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> His funeral, at <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen&#39;s Cathedral, Vienna">St. Stephen\'s Cathedral</a> in Vienna, was attended by many prominent Formula One figures (including <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Berger" title="Gerhard Berger">Gerhard Berger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Stewart" title="Jackie Stewart">Jackie Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alain_Prost" title="Alain Prost">Alain Prost</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Piquet" title="Nelson Piquet">Nelson Piquet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Alesi" title="Jean Alesi">Jean Alesi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Vettel" title="Sebastian Vettel">Sebastian Vettel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Coulthard" title="David Coulthard">David Coulthard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nico_Rosberg" title="Nico Rosberg">Nico Rosberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Valtteri_Bottas" title="Valtteri Bottas">Valtteri Bottas</a>), <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a>, and many Austrian politicians, including <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Van_der_Bellen" title="Alexander Van der Bellen">Alexander Van der Bellen</a> among others.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Haas_VF-19" title="Haas VF-19">Haas VF-19</a>\'s mini shark fin section of the engine cover (the top) was painted red with Lauda\'s name and his years of birth and death. Both <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Vettel" title="Sebastian Vettel">Sebastian Vettel</a> wore special helmets in remembrance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Lauda is widely considered to be one of the greatest F1 drivers of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Racing_record">Racing record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Racing record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_summary">Career summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Niki_Lauda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit
